  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_895ee3c4-7d9c-4a20-80c1-e865aa0a09b9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer1238572448216704968"><i>Older cover edition of ASIN <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18392290-the-tied-man' rel='nofollow noopener'>B00AXDNVHS</a></i><br/><br/><br/>Lilith Bresson, an independent, successful young artist, is forced to travel from her home in Spain to the wild borderlands of northern England, to repay her feckless father’s latest debt by painting a portrait of the enigmatic Lady Blaine Albermarle.<br/><br/>On her first night at Albermarle Hall she meets Finn Strachan, Blaine’s ‘companion’, a</span>
  <span id="freeText1238572448216704968" style="display:none"><i>Older cover edition of ASIN <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18392290-the-tied-man" rel="nofollow noopener">B00AXDNVHS</a></i><br /><br /><br />Lilith Bresson, an independent, successful young artist, is forced to travel from her home in Spain to the wild borderlands of northern England, to repay her feckless father’s latest debt by painting a portrait of the enigmatic Lady Blaine Albermarle.<br /><br />On her first night at Albermarle Hall she meets Finn Strachan, Blaine’s ‘companion’, a cultured and hauntingly beautiful young man who seems to have it all. But Lilith has an artist’s eye, and a gift for seeing what lies beneath the skin. She soon discovers that Blaine is more gaoler than lover, and if the price is right, depravity has no limits.<br /><br />As the weeks pass, Lilith finds that she too is drawn into the malign web that her patron has spun, yet against the odds she forges a strong friendship with the damaged, dysfunctional Finn. In a dark, modern twist to an age-old story, Lilith Bresson proves that sometimes it’s the princess who needs to become the rescuer.<br /><br />Please note that this storyline contains depictions of drug abuse, violence and non-consensual sexual activity.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/138007-i-m-not-sure-what-i-feel-for-henry-was-he">I&#39;m not sure what I feel for Henry. Was he a good guy or bad? On the surface, he seemed kind and timid. On the other hand, he was a complete and utter weasel! I am having trouble forming a true opinion of him.</a>
</div>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/16819540-tabitha-mcgowan"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1442657399i/16819540._UX100_CR0,25,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/16819540-tabitha-mcgowan">Tabitha McGowan</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think for me, Henry is just human. He's not strong, or particularly brave (although he gets braver), but he's trapped and isolated. He didn't do wha<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think for me, Henry is just human. He's not strong, or particularly brave (although he gets braver), but he's trapped and isolated. He didn't do what he did out of malice, but the end result for Finn and Lilith was the same, regardless of intentions. I like that he's quite an ambiguous character for so many people! I like to think he's stronger now too, seeing as he's got his first proper boyfriend.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer561774958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4067257710887010532"><br/>***THIS REVIEW ISN’T FOR YOU LIGHT-HEARTERS OUT THERE. THIS IS A VERY CRUDE REVIEW. AND IT ESPECIALLY ISN’T FOR ANYONE BELOW THE AGE OF EIGHTEEN.***<br/><br/><a href='http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/ac296d875e0625ad0d255514f2a8ee45.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814194._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo ac296d875e0625ad0d255514f2a8ee45.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>♦ <b>Such a beautiful story.</b> ♦<br/><br/>This is a book that’s going to take you out of your comfort zone, guys. I’m going to tell you that <b>right now</b>. So before you read <i>The Tied Man</i>, I want you to pick out a quiet and very dark corner in your home.<br/><br/><b>Because you’re going to need it to rock yourself to sleep later.</b><br/><br/>The thing about this book that nailed me right be</span>
  <span id="freeText4067257710887010532" style="display:none"><br>***THIS REVIEW ISN’T FOR YOU LIGHT-HEARTERS OUT THERE. THIS IS A VERY CRUDE REVIEW. AND IT ESPECIALLY ISN’T FOR ANYONE BELOW THE AGE OF EIGHTEEN.***<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/ac296d875e0625ad0d255514f2a8ee45.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814194._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo ac296d875e0625ad0d255514f2a8ee45.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>♦ <b>Such a beautiful story.</b> ♦<br><br>This is a book that’s going to take you out of your comfort zone, guys. I’m going to tell you that <b>right now</b>. So before you read <i>The Tied Man</i>, I want you to pick out a quiet and very dark corner in your home.<br><br><b>Because you’re going to need it to rock yourself to sleep later.</b><br><br>The thing about this book that nailed me right between the eyes… was that it WAS such a beautiful story. And I couldn’t stop reading it even if I tried! And it’s built on the lesson that teaches us that <b>sometimes</b>… friendship between two people is <b>far</b> more intimate than even the most perverse sexual act. <br><br>Quintessentially, this story has <b>three</b> main characters. A world-famed artist, <b>Lilith Bressen</b>, is primarily introduced when she’s agreed to venture off to Albermarle Hall to paint the portrait of the lady of the house, <b>Blaine Albermarle</b>. Upon arrival, Lilith meets Blaine and her “companion”, <b>Finn Strachan</b>.<br><br><b>
  <i>I had never met anyone quite like the willow-thin young man standing before me: Finn had the face of a fallen angel.<br><br>Wide, dissolute eyes the colour of moss agate gazed out from behind a long, thick fringe of muddy blond hair, and loose strands fell to frame a snub nose and sensuous cupid’s bow of a mouth that was just saved from being feminine by a square, stubborn jaw.<br><br>The very first time I met him, Finn Strachan stole my breath.</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/8eb4153856dae66129957dfe2d7b1520.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814195._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 8eb4153856dae66129957dfe2d7b1520.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>And thence, the games begin…</i><br><br>Right away, Lilith knows that something uncanny is afoot. She can’t quite place her finger on it, but she knows something’s not quite right when Finn gives her a sexual proposal. However… it’s not the proposal that sets up a red flag… <br><br>It’s the robotic way in which he proposes it. <br><br>♦Like it’s second nature to him. <br>Like he does it everyday.♦<br>♦With every guest.<br><br>And because Lilith has a very shrewd artistic eye… suddenly Finn’s haunted eyes, beautiful face, and a body laden with bruises begin to make sense.<br><br>Especially when Blaine gives the suspension away by telling Lilith that Finn isn’t merely her “companion”… but rather her <b>employee</b> she uses to entertain her guests. <br><br>And by entertainment for guests… I mean Finn is <b>sexually exploited</b> by her guests.<br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/6a9d8eeb152f9df59dd6748e34449992.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814196._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 6a9d8eeb152f9df59dd6748e34449992.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And he’s not used just for the women: he’s used for the men as well. And for the perverse. And for the sinister who have a liking for beating the living <b>shit</b> out of Finn while they get off. <br><br><b>
  <i> Finn’s face contorted in agony as a clenched hand was shoved deep into him, and when Ellis pulled his fingers away blood and shit glistened across his knuckles. He must have deemed him ready, because without any further ceremony he began to fuck Finn with legal savagery.<br><br>Chester was the first to roll away from Finn's battered body, spend and happy, as Ellis brought himself to one last heaving climax above their plaything's bowed and insensible head. He grinned with obscene joy as he came, leaving viscous strings of semen to drip over Finn's hair and shoulders.<br><br>When it was all over, they embraced and raised their glasses to each other as they congratulated themselves on living out their sordid fantasy.</i>
</b><br><br>All of which happens just so Blaine can watch.<br><br>See, Blaine’s the <b>villain</b> in this story. And it would be a <b>vast</b> understatement to say that she’s a sociopathic villain with an affinity for voyeurism. <br><br>She’s a sick, <i>sick</i>, <b>sick</b> woman.<br><br>Let’s see… how can I drive the point home as to how menacingly malicious this woman is?<br><br><b>Okay.</b><br><br>She’s the kind of woman who would kill you while she let you listen to your favorite song. She’s the kind of woman who could strangle you with a feather. She’s the kind of woman who would inject dye into your eye with an eight-inch needle just to see if the iris would change color.<br><br><b>Just for shits and giggles.</b><br><br>And Lilith doesn’t notice it when she arrives at Albermarle Hall, but she has just fallen face-first into life-long game of sexual depravity.<br><br><b>And Finn is the star-player.</b><br><br>After she finds out what exactly Finn <i>does</i>, Lilith is completely appalled by both him <i>and</i> Blaine. But because Lilith is forced to stay until she completes the painting… she soon learns that Finn really isn’t a player in the scheme of things, but rather the <b>victim</b>. Because he, too, is there against his will. <br><br>And what’s truly beautiful about this story, is the relationship Lilith and Finn form. For awhile, they sort of dance around the other. Because here’s <i>Lilith</i>, a Fort Knox of a young woman who’s quite guarded… and then here’s <i>Finn</i> who has no personal security whatsoever because he’s literally had everything <b>stripped</b> from him. And soon they form this comradery that turns into their understanding each other that turns into their protecting each other that turns into their <b>loving</b> each other.<br><br>But what they <b>don’t</b> know… is that Blaine, the voyeur that she is… is watching all of this happen.<br><br><b>
  <i> “Pull back, Finn. For both your sakes.”<br><br>“I can take it.”<br><br>“You might be able to...”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/tumblr_m3bdf7Svnp1qcq4ago1_400-1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814197.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_m3bdf7Svnp1qcq4ago1_400-1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>
  <b> But can Lilith?” </b>
</i><br><br>***<u>Reviewer’s Note:</u>***<br><br><i>I think, essentially, what made this book so consuming for me was the fact that Tabitha McGowan *told* it so well. There’s a distinctive grace to her writing that’s so compelling. And while reading it… it’s definitely safe to say that this is a story that only <b>she</b> could tell. It’s hard to have such a crude basis as part of a plot design and be able to tell it with such refinement. But she did. In spades.<br><br>And I, without a question, recommend this book to anyone and everyone. Especially those who aren’t afraid to feel a LOT of impact while reading. And by that… I mean get ready to be *sucker-punched* by this story.<br><br><b>Now if you'll excuse me...</b></i><br><br><a href="http://s59.photobucket.com/user/ashleeporte/media/XjiqQ.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380413483i/814198.jpg" alt=" photo XjiqQ.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><br></span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1250911442?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1250911442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3857953767503429991"><strong>A Tale Of Unspeakable Depravity</strong><br/><br/>For years, Finn has been the unwilling entertainment for 100s of cruel and twisted clients. Coerced into selling himself by a wealthy Englishwoman, he must submit to the perverse whims of a steady stream of strangers or else risk the safety of his two younger sisters. <br/><br/>However sadistic the customers may be, Finn has yet to encounter one that was crueler than his boss/owner, Blaine. She gets off on hurting him, both physically and emotionally. While she uses threats </span>
  <span id="freeText3857953767503429991" style="display:none"><strong>A Tale Of Unspeakable Depravity</strong><br /><br />For years, Finn has been the unwilling entertainment for 100s of cruel and twisted clients. Coerced into selling himself by a wealthy Englishwoman, he must submit to the perverse whims of a steady stream of strangers or else risk the safety of his two younger sisters. <br /><br />However sadistic the customers may be, Finn has yet to encounter one that was crueler than his boss/owner, Blaine. She gets off on hurting him, both physically and emotionally. While she uses threats and blackmail to maintain power, she has a special interest in Finn and is constantly dreaming up ways to toy with him. His life is a living hell.<br /><br />Lilith first arrives at the mysterious island "retreat" after being coerced by her father, who failed to pay his tab. Apparently, Blaine wants a portrait by Lilith, a famous painter, and demands this as payment for her father's debt.<br /><br />Soon, Lilith finds herself trapped on the island. It doesn't take her long to figure out that she is a pawn in Blaine's sick games. Unable to stop Blaine's appalling abuse of Finn, she finds herself growing fonder of him and walking a dangerous line. <br /><br />This story was heart-breaking, shocking and deeply emotional. My heart went out to Finn, and to a lesser extent Lilith. Blaine's cruelty knew no bounds. She was cunning, beautiful...and a total sociopath! The fear was almost palpable.<br /><br />I would recommend this story to anyone that enjoys a dark romance. It was a little slow-moving at first, but once the story got going, I couldn't put it down. The ending seemed a bit rushed and I really wanted more of Finn and Lilith post-Blaire. If it weren't for the rushed ending, it probably would've been a 5-star read for me.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer1198940527905480675"><br/><b>Some of my emotions while reading this story:</b><br/><p>

  <br/>

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410309ra/804357.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>

  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410309ra/804358.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>

It was dark and disturbing to the max, but at the same time it was so eloquent and beautifully written that I ended up loving it to pieces. The topics that are addressed in this novel aren't the most conventional ones, but that's exactly what makes the story so unique. The author does not make an effort to hide the ugliest aspects of life and inst</p></span>
  <span id="freeText1198940527905480675" style="display:none"><br><b>Some of my emotions while reading this story:</b><br><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/679665.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>

  <br>
</p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/623300.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>

</p><p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410309ra/804359.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>WOW.</b><br><br>This book was <i>unlike</i> anything I've EVER read. It was dark and disturbing to the max, but at the same time it was so eloquent and beautifully written that I ended up loving it to pieces. The topics that are addressed in this novel aren't the most conventional ones, but that's exactly what makes the story so unique. The author does not make an effort to hide the ugliest aspects of life and instead, chooses to depict those aspects in detail. But by doing that, the beautiful and peaceful moments in life suddenly seem all the more valuable and worth fighting for.<br><br>PS: the story also consists of one of the most cruel, sadistic female characters I've ever come across: <b>Blaine Albermarle...</b><br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410309ra/804360.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410309ra/804361.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Oh, and <b>Coyle O'Halloran</b> too, for that matter...</i><br><br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~<br><br>At the beginning of the story we meet a young man named, <b>Finn Strachan.</b> with the face of a fallen angel, Finn manages to enrapture everyone upon meeting them.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804362._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But behind the beautiful facade, there's a lot of darkness and pain.<br><br></p><blockquote>
<b>"The summer I met Lilith Bresson, I had begun to die. Not physically, you understand. I had never been that lucky. But each day a little more of my soul disappeared and Blaine sensed it. <br><br>And Blaine Albermarle never let anything escape without a fight."</b> ~ Finn</blockquote><br><br>Finn's life is in full control of the lady that rules Albermarle Hall, where he lives. A lady named Blaine Albermarle. She rules every aspect of his life and makes him entertain her numerous guests in any possible way. His life has been stripped of every sense of freedom. He's a <i>tied man</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804363._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When famous and eccentric artist <b>Lilith Bresson</b> gets the assignment to leave her home and warm surroundings in Spain to visit Albermarle Hall in a cold and dreary village in England, she never expected her life to change that dramatically. Dreading a stay in her home country, she decides to make a quick job of painting the infamous Blaine Albermarle. But the moment she meets Finn Starchan, she has a feeling her life has changed for good and she realizes she might not be able to leave that soon after all.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>"Control. The one thing that shaped my life, and the one that I felt I was about to lose."</b> ~ Lilith</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804364.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<b>"But at the end of the day, everything costs me. The only question is how much."</b> ~ Finn</blockquote><br><br>As the story progresses, Finn and Lilith begin to form a close bond and friendship. And soon, they're united in their shared hatred towards the cruelties that take place in and around Albermarle Hall, most of which the same person is responsable for: Blaine. But she's not the only one who makes his life miserable... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804365.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The things Finn has to go through are downright horrible. There's just no other way to describe them. I sometimes had to take a break from reading just because it got too intense and heartbreaking and all I wanted was for him to finally find peace and be happy, but each moment of hapiness was followed by one of utter dispair.<br><br><blockquote>
<b>"You're not okay, Finn. In fact, I'd say you were about as far from 'okay' as a human being could get right now, short of being dead."</b> ~ Lilith</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804366.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lilith seems to be the only person who can make Finn feel alive again. But will her friendship and comfort be enough? Will it be enough to finally set Finn free or will he be forever bound by the cruel bonds and rules that Blaine Albermarle applies...<br><br><blockquote>
<b>"The momentary discomfort was nothing at all compared to the realisation that she was finding comfort in my flawed embrace."</b> ~ Finn</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804367.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I don't expect you to be like them. Don't want you to be. It's not them I want, it's you. From the moment we met, it's only been you." ♥♥</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Overall, The Tied Man is by far one of the most unique, shocking, captivating, memorable and beautiful stories I've read and it easily deserves to be on my all time favorite list. This story might not be for everyone, but if you can manage to get past the more cruel and harsh aspects of the story, then I would highly advise you to give it a try! <br><br>I was really happy with the way the story ended, but all it did was leave me wanting more... I loved both Finn and Lilith and their beautifully flawed, yet strong personalities, so I'm already anxiously looking forward to the next part of their story in <i>The Tied Man - Unbound</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410309i/804368.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"What did you call me?"<br><br>"Ah. A chuisle. Gaelic. 'My darling'. I prefer the proper translation, mind you."<br><br>"Which is?"<br><br>He gave a bashful smile. "My pulse."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="1198940527905480675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3504255640" />
    <a title="Giorgia ~ Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/97546350-giorgia-reads"><img alt="Giorgia ~ Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597878668p2/97546350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3504255640?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giorgia ~ Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giorgia ~ Reads" href="/user/show/97546350-giorgia-reads">Giorgia ~ Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18392290-the-tied-man">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=dark-themes">dark-themes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/97546350-giorgia-reads?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3504255640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14681090147156672192"><b> 4 stars </b> <br/><br/>It took me awhile to decide what to rate this and although it will be one that will stay with me <i>(just one of those you don’t forget)</i>, I couldn’t rate it any higher because I do think it was a bit too much at times and it emotionally exhausted me! I flinched, felt nauseated and disturbed beyond what I can explain with words. <br/><br/>Is there a question of whether this was good or bad? No, cause it was definitely very good. Both writing and story. <br/><br/>It’s more along the lines of how much dark is t</span>
  <span id="freeText14681090147156672192" style="display:none"><b> 4 stars </b> <br /><br />It took me awhile to decide what to rate this and although it will be one that will stay with me <i>(just one of those you don’t forget)</i>, I couldn’t rate it any higher because I do think it was a bit too much at times and it emotionally exhausted me! I flinched, felt nauseated and disturbed beyond what I can explain with words. <br /><br />Is there a question of whether this was good or bad? No, cause it was definitely very good. Both writing and story. <br /><br />It’s more along the lines of how much dark is too much dark? <br /><br />I’m not a voracious reader of dark/twisted romance. I like them but I need a balance of dark and normal. Along with that, there are certain things I cannot tolerate. But the most important thing for me when I pick a dark read is that the main romantic relationship to be a healthy one. I can’t tolerate when the MC’s are abusive to each other emotionally or in any other form. Basically the dark part of the book needs to be an external thing to the relationship. <br /><br />Now, <b>this book meets my criteria</b> but damn... I felt nauseous, disgusted, heartbroken, angry and I can go on and on. It was one of the hardest books I’ve read, that’s not saying much since as I’ve mentioned, I don’t read a lot of dark romance but when I do I’m used to reading dark books which are less explicit, or in which the trauma/abuse is perhaps depicted but not in present time, and we are not going through it at the same time with the characters. And if that is a scenario which does happen it’s not prolonged the way it was in this. <br /><br />The relationship between the leads tho, God, that was beautiful. And the way everything unfolded, the writing itself as well as the character development, it was all done very well. <br /><br />To be honest I kinda knew what this was about and how it was gonna unfold because I read some reviews beforehand. Now, what those reviews didn’t really explain (ok, maybe they did, but I didn’t take it very seriously) was how hard this was going to be to read. For anyone who might wanna pick this up: <b> Read the reviews </b> and get all the spoilers (non-plot related) to decide if it’s for you. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14681090147156672192" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_543061612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543061612" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543061612?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      Buddy read w/Crystal, Rebecca, Joan, Amanda, Carina (and a recap w/Ash!)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=romantica-or-erotica">romantica-or-erotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=bdsm-or-person-in-control">bdsm-or-person-in-control</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=dark-or-taboo">dark-or-taboo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543061612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10951031655714697148"><b>This is one of the most disturbing books I have ever read.</b> My heart was broken over and over. I had a hard time knowing how to react other than to feel completely disturbed and lament on how I'd been put through the ringer. Could I reward a story with a high rating if it turned my stomach over and over?<br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Two hundred and twelve breaths.<br/>That's how long it took me to risk moving again.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><b>4.25 stars.</b> Don't judge a book by its cover is an overused statement, but also completely appropriate her</span>
  <span id="freeText10951031655714697148" style="display:none"><b>This is one of the most disturbing books I have ever read.</b> My heart was broken over and over. I had a hard time knowing how to react other than to feel completely disturbed and lament on how I'd been put through the ringer. Could I reward a story with a high rating if it turned my stomach over and over?<br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Two hundred and twelve breaths.<br />That's how long it took me to risk moving again.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>4.25 stars.</b> Don't judge a book by its cover is an overused statement, but also completely appropriate here. The writing in <i>The Tied Man</i> was impressive. The style almost felt like British literary fiction, until the story suddenly decided to take a turn into the realm of something dark and twisted. My notes in the book say, "when literary fiction drives into a ditch." That's about it right there.<br /><br />This is the story of one man trapped by a woman who chooses to sell him over and over to be abused in any fashion which the purchaser(s) may prefer. This is also the story of a woman who found this damaged man and lost her heart to a situation which may be broken beyond repair. <br /><br />Did I say already that this book broke my heart?<br /><br /><b>I was shocked.<br />I was horrified.<br />I was disgusted.<br />I was moved.<br />I was hopeful.<br />I was on the edge of my seat (okay, bed...I lounge when I read).<br />I did not like this book.<br />I am already telling people to read it.</b><br /><br />Are you confused about my "did not like" statement and how it conflicts with my rating? Let me explain : the book was depraved, yet it was an engaging read. I can't write words of joy, or exclaim love for something which made me feel horrible. Yet, I do not regret reading. As well, I do appreciate the author's ability to draw me in to the story.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I might have just lost something that wasn't mine to begin with.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This was a well-written book that I couldn't stop reading. But I won't represent it with gushing or flashy pictures because that cheapens the experience for me, and turns the book into something less serious than what it is. The reason why this book had such an effect on me is because darkness only gave way to more darkness. So a dancing hippo and pretty font headers won't truly show how this book got into my head.<br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>An hour and a half was all I'd wanted - ninety poxy minutes with a woman who was content to share my company without leaving the kind of souvenir that required medical attention.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br />If you've read dark erotica before featuring rape, abuse, or slavery, be prepared to have your mind taken to another level. And that's all I will say about that.<br /><br />Even though the majority of <i>The Tied Man</i> was full of nothing but torment, there was a small slice of hope. It wasn't pretty hope or romantic hope, but it was still a form of love in rare beauty. This is what humanized the story and turned it into something worth reading. So if you're afraid to pick up this book, let me leave you with a passage which might make you change your mind.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"What did you call me?"<br />"Ah. A chuisle. Gaelic. 'My darling.' I prefer the proper translation, mind you."<br />"Which is?"<br />He gave a bashful smile. "My pulse."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10951031655714697148" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

</a><br/><b>
  <i>“Just o</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText15390100236786507828" style="display:none"><b>5 Phenomenal Stars!!!!! </b><br><br>This is not an easy book to review... It wasn’t an easy book to read. All of the heartbreak and devastation was worth it. Such a beautiful story with characters you will fall in love with, and other characters you will despise. Here goes nothing...<br><br>This was a story about an artist named Lilith <br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/531c7e28-8724-4cda-9b1b-af18a283f123_zps58f6cbaa.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <i>“Just out of interest, what did you make of my Finn?”<br> “Probably the most beautiful man I’ve ever seen.”</i>
</b><br><br>Finn is living as Blaine’s ‘companion’ but thats not the whole story... Finn is trapped. He is pretty much forced to do whatever Blaine and her guests want and if he doesn’t there are consequences. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/fa307f65-8b24-40bc-9745-3e06a297a2ad_zpsb90a0d35.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807294.jpg" alt=" photo fa307f65-8b24-40bc-9745-3e06a297a2ad_zpsb90a0d35.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This doesn’t sit well with Lili. She and Finn develop a friendship. Blaine is not happy that Lili won’t give in to her, but she won’t take advantage of Finn. Finn only does what he does because he has to. Blaine has this way of manipulating everyone. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ She holds the only people dear to Finn over his head, his two sisters. She does the same to Lil with her little brother. She is so evil!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><blockquote>
<b><i>“Y’ know what my job is, huh? It’s to say ‘Yes’ and keep saying it until whoever’s paying decides they’ve had enough. It doesn’t matter if I’m not happy, or if it disgusts me, or even if it hurts like I’d rather fucking die. So deal with it. I have to.”</i></b> </blockquote><br><br>Finn will break your heart. I had to take frequent breaks while reading this, it all got to be too much for me. If you are anything like me, there will be tears and wine involved. <br><br>Lili wants nothing more than to help Finn. She develops stronger feelings for him and feels her control slipping. Soon, Blaine realizes this and uses it against her.<br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/db34134f-91cc-4819-8b0b-b2610106cdb1_zps7b8dec52.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807295.jpg" alt=" photo db34134f-91cc-4819-8b0b-b2610106cdb1_zps7b8dec52.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Lilith knows there is something special about Finn, and if he is forced to continue this life, it will break him. He deserves so much more than the hand he has been dealt. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> “You deserve better.”<br><br>“Lili- no ones ever done anything like this for me. Ever. Are you hearing me? I sure as hell know I wouldn’t have taken the risks you did today just for a whore.” <br>“Don’t say that.” <br>“It’s what I am.” <br>“It’s what she makes you do. It’s not who you are.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Finn is broken, but Lili gives him strength. I will never forget these two... such memorable characters. Lili is strong and independent. I really loved how she handled things, especially at the end. She never gave up on Finn. Finn was sweet, kind, and funny. He was also helpless, hopeless and depressed. Lili gave him help, hope and happiness. Such a beautiful story. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/8857d810-e804-4bc9-bb6e-c6a7aa8fb718_zps5d938f19.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807296.jpg" alt=" photo 8857d810-e804-4bc9-bb6e-c6a7aa8fb718_zps5d938f19.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I can guarantee that as much as you love Lilith and Finn (and you will LOVE Lili and Finn) you will HATE Blaine. Worst, most terribly disgusting character ever! Tabitha really knows how to right a villain!!! Coyle is a second runner up... they are both all kinds of awful! <br><br>While reading, you will have to repeat this to yourself over and over, I found myself constantly forgetting:<br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/GIFS/GIFS5_zpsc0900bb7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807297.jpg" alt=" photo GIFS5_zpsc0900bb7.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This one gutted me. Parts of this book, I felt destroyed. I stayed up half the night reading, then I had trouble sleeping because I couldn’t get Finn and Lilith out of my head. It was terrible. One of the most intense books I have ever read. This book made me feel... I don’t even know how to describe it.<br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/GIFS/gif-eos1_zps7d86dbab.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380383940ra/742352.gif" alt=" photo gif-eos1_zps7d86dbab.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> I do know that I will be recommending it to everyone! It is a must read, and towards the top of my favorites shelf!<br><br>My favorite line in the book....<br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/28d2d161-e2c0-4bd2-a08f-f270b4c94d97_zps77f7be15.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807298.jpg" alt=" photo 28d2d161-e2c0-4bd2-a08f-f270b4c94d97_zps77f7be15.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>My ONLY complaint about this book has now been deemed useless... I was going to say, even though I loved the ending, I wish we would have gotten an epilogue or something, but now there is a second book coming out which is even better!!! If you haven’t picked this one up, you need to!!! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/d5d1b9c7-97f0-49eb-8607-85466d0b4ed0_zpsb7c43ecf.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411251i/807299.jpg" alt=" photo d5d1b9c7-97f0-49eb-8607-85466d0b4ed0_zpsb7c43ecf.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15390100236786507828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_727187167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/727187167" />
    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/727187167?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer727187167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5797649331011063890"><br/> <b>4.5 SOLID STARS</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b> The summer I met Lilith Bresson, I had begun to die. Not physically, you understand. I had never been that lucky. But each day a little more of my soul disappeared, and Blaine sensed it.</b>
</blockquote><br/>Wow, this was a bit of a rollercoaster ride. But I made it! Thanks Shannon for recommending this one to me. It was dark but I think I had a fair idea that it was going to be before reading it so maybe it was not as shocking as others who read it without any hint of the storyline etc.<br/><br/>First off</span>
  <span id="freeText5797649331011063890" style="display:none"><br> <b>4.5 SOLID STARS</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b> The summer I met Lilith Bresson, I had begun to die. Not physically, you understand. I had never been that lucky. But each day a little more of my soul disappeared, and Blaine sensed it.</b>
</blockquote><br>Wow, this was a bit of a rollercoaster ride. But I made it! Thanks Shannon for recommending this one to me. It was dark but I think I had a fair idea that it was going to be before reading it so maybe it was not as shocking as others who read it without any hint of the storyline etc.<br><br>First off let me just say, as they might say in Ireland ….<br><br>Finn, weren't you the right<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885052._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>to land yourself in a load of shite like that.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"How shite was my childhood - a True Story by yet another Irish White-Trash Bastard."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Yeah, Finn's childhood was not good so maybe he thought he was going to live the life of Reilly when he met up with Lady Albermarle. Boy, was he wrong!<br><br>Albermarle Hall …<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885053._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Yes, this peaceful, kind, world is set in the rolling hills of Northumberland …. <b> NOT!</b> … peaceful and kind, I mean.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885054._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>FINN STRACHAN</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885055._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b> The very first time I met him, Finn Strachan stole my breath</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b> LILITH BRESSON</b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885056._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Lilith is a famous artist who is brought to the Hall to paint the Lady of the Manor's portrait.<br><blockquote>
  <b>"Just out of interest, what did you make of my Finn?"<br><br>"Probably the most beautiful man I've ever seen."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I usually reserve the <b>"C"</b> word for those totally unworthy to live in this world, the scum of the earth, the lowlifes who have no redeeming features. Was there someone like that in this book. Sure there was - Lady Blaine Albermarle - one word - <b>"Cunt"</b>, actually two words, <b>"Fucking Cunt"</b>! She was a prize bitch. She had taken Finn from the streets of Dublin and was keeping him against his will. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885057._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And her friends were just as bad.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Lady Albermarle to you isn’t it, you Paddy piece of shit.”</b>
</blockquote><br>What a dick he was. I first visited London about 25 years ago and definitely felt a bit of an anti-Irish vibe there, in some places, pubs, not everywhere mind you. I felt so self conscious with my Irish accent. Did actually get referred to as a "Paddy" by one nice chap. At least at that stage there were no signs for job advertisements saying, "NO IRISH NEED APPLY". Thank God that day is gone. Back then the Troubles in Northern Ireland were still potent but again, that has changed for the better. Some of my best friends are British, you know who you are you Slappers!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“It was easy to forget that other people lived in a world where rules and laws and common sense could keep you safe. A world where, if you did the right thing you were allowed to get on with your life in whichever way you chose.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885058._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>"I trust Coyle gave you a warm welcome."<br>"He was very professional."<br>"He normally receives better reports than that, especially from our female guests. Was there a problem?"<br>"No, no problem. It's just - well, he knows it doesn't he? That whole 'Celtic Charm' thing's a well-polished act, but reminded me of one of those theme pubs on the Dublin tourist trail. Shelves full of pitchforks and wheelbarrows, and not a native in sight."</b>
</blockquote><br>He <i> HAD</i> to be Irish, hadn't he?!! Seriously what a Prick he was. He was not just mean, he was bad to the core - dickhead.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885059._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Henry, wanted to throttle you at one stage too.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"What did you call me?"<br><br>"Ah. A chuisle. Gaelic. 'My darling'. I prefer the proper translation, mind you."<br><br>"Which is?"<br><br>He gave a bashful smile. "My pulse."</b>
</blockquote><br>Well, you learn something new every day. I studied Irish/Gaelic for 13 years - it is compulsory in Ireland - still not bloody fluent in it. Often heard the expression "chuisle" - never knew that it translated as "pulse".<br><br>The stuff that Finn had to endure was awful. He was drugged up half the time so that he could endure the suffering. But when those two arrived, seriously, they were the fucking icing on the cake. Horrible<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437714i/885060.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“In a fortnight Lilith had figured out more about me than anyone had ever cared to know, and I could only hope that she would hold it gently.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>The last part of the book was a real rollercoaster - would they, could they?<br>I could feel my blood pressure rising wanting it all to end well. But there were still a few surprises in store.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380437714ra/885061.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This is a debut novel by this author. Was a bit wary as I read that she is English and wasn't sure if she would portray the Irish character as realistic. I have been burned before, reading about Ireland and Irish characters where we are made out to be living in the back arse of nowhere with accents like Tom Cruise in Far and Away. But I cannot mention any authors as we all have to be nice and friendly here on Goodreads. No author bashing allowed. But I needn't have worried. Finn was great, the real deal - had the Irish expressions down to a tee.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"feckin'"</i>
    <br>
    <br>
    <i>"… thought I was the dog's bollocks"</i>
    <br>
    <br>
    <i>"away with the fairies"</i>
    <br>
    <br>
    <i>"Jesus, you look knackered"</i>
    <br>
    <br>
    <i>"No, it was shite"</i>
    <br>
    <br>
    <i>"Shut your filthy fuckin' hole"</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I am not sure how much of a reputation the Irish have of using bad language. We do use it, a lot. It is not nice. I have lived outside Ireland for more than 24 years and I remember being on holiday there some years back and the oldest said to me "Why does everyone use the "F" word?" Because I grew up with it I suppose I was tuned out and did not really notice but when I did tune back in, it was all over the place, in the pub, walking down the street, at the football and hurling matches. I suppose the only place you will not hear it is at Mass. I still use bad language - I really should try not to but I just cannot help myself.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“Even at this ridiculous hour, and clad in a faded blue t-shirt and ancient pyjama pants, he looked like something Michelangelo might reject for being too beautiful”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>And she got the accents right on the names and words …<br><br><b>Sinēad<br><br>Sláinte</b><br><br>I have a son called Seán and every time I see his name written by a teacher or whoever without the "sīne fada", it drives me demented. Being, Irish, I think I am entitled to nit-pick a little bit.<br><br>I did want an Epilogue - the ending was way too abrupt for me. But I guess it paves the way for a future story for Finn Strachen and Lilith Bresson.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I can’t do this alone, Finn. I need you beside me.”<br>“Nobody had ever said that to me.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5797649331011063890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1376334163?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="warhawke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="warhawke" href="/user/show/25494927-warhawke">warhawke</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1376334163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18171664871959957258"><b>Type: </b> Standalone book 1 of The Tied Man series<br/><b>POV: </b> First Person - Dual<br/><b>Rating: </b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423545558i/13641856.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441032155i/16054096.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Lilith Bresson was a famous artist forced to return to her homeland to repay her father’s debt by doing a painting for Lady Blaine Albermarle. She was invited as a guess at Albermarle Hall not knowing the true horror hiding behind the luxurious gateway façade. <br/><br/>Finn Strachan was Lady Albermarle’s handsome young companion. Behind the prim and proper persona, he was a man desperate for any kind of escape he could manage</span>
  <span id="freeText18171664871959957258" style="display:none"><b>Type: </b> Standalone book 1 of The Tied Man series<br><b>POV: </b> First Person - Dual<br><b>Rating: </b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423545558i/13641856.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441032155i/16054096.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lilith Bresson was a famous artist forced to return to her homeland to repay her father’s debt by doing a painting for Lady Blaine Albermarle. She was invited as a guess at Albermarle Hall not knowing the true horror hiding behind the luxurious gateway façade. <br><br>Finn Strachan was Lady Albermarle’s handsome young companion. Behind the prim and proper persona, he was a man desperate for any kind of escape he could manage. But Lilith’s arrival brought in complications he didn’t see coming.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423265644i/13602509.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What first caught my attention about this book was the unconventional role of the hero and heroine. It’s not something you find a lot among the chock-full of alpha heroes on bookshelves. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>‘Y’know what my job is, huh? It’s to say ‘Yes’ and keep saying it until whoever’s paying decides they’ve had enough. It doesn’t matter if I’m not happy, or if it disgusts me, or even if it hurts like I’d rather fucking die. So deal with it. I have to.’</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I think it’s impossible for anyone not to love Finn. He was a helpless victim but that didn’t make him weak. It took strength to endure the things he had to as long as he did. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441032155i/16054097.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It took me a while to warm up to Lilith. She was a fierce, independent female character, but she could also be abrasive at times. What I love about her is that she knew when to fight and when to be docile. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>In my long and illustrious career I had been fucked by a procession of evil bastards, but none ever quite matched the sublime cruelty of Blaine. </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I think it’s been a long time since I truly hated a character and Blaine earned her place in this one. And she hardly even lifted a finger.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>‘And that means the less of this... kind of thing there is, the easier it’ll be for you. Sometimes the more you have, the more you’ll miss it when it’s gone.’</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I love the secondary characters, Henry, Gabriel and Nat, each in its own way. I love Nat since the beginning and I was so angry with Lilith at how she treated him.<br><br>The story flowed at a good pace and I don’t think it’s that dark. I mean there were some horrifying scenes that would be hard for those with gentler heart/stomach to read, but the overall feel was lighter than I expected. There were also some funny bits scattered throughout the book. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“But at the end of the day, everything I do costs me. The only question is how much.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>What I love the most about this book is the friendship between Finn and Lilith. I didn’t see The Tied Man as a love story. I saw it as a story of friendship and sacrifices. And it certainly not erotic. There were explicit scenes but it wasn’t meant to titillate. Instead it was used to show the horror and the depravity of Albermarle Hall. <br><br>Personally, one thing I found to be a bit of a challenge was the writing. There were a lot of British words and slangs that I’m not familiar with and I had to constantly refer to dictionary and Google. I also wish there was more to Finn’s background. <br><br>For the ending, I might be among the very few who actually love it ended that way. I would be perfectly content with it but of course I would still read book 2 when it comes out. <br><br>The Tied Man was a story of two individuals who formed a beautiful relationship by feeding off each other’s strength to survive physical and psychological assaults. It is recommended to those looking for an unconventional story and don’t mind delving into the depraved world of sexual slavery. <br><br><b>Note:</b><br><i>The Tied Man is a complete story that can be read on its own.<br>Books in the series: </i><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17237477.The_Tied_Man__The_Tied_Man___1_" title="The Tied Man (The Tied Man, #1) by Tabitha McGowan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1377634218s/17237477.jpg" alt="The Tied Man (The Tied Man, #1) by Tabitha McGowan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17662480.The_Tied_Man_Unbound__The_Tied_Man___2_" title="The Tied Man Unbound (The Tied Man, #2) by Tabitha McGowan" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/book/50x75-a91bf249278a81aabab721ef782c4a74.png" alt="The Tied Man Unbound (The Tied Man, #2) by Tabitha McGowan" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For more reviews/reveals/giveaways visit:<br><a href="http://warhawkevault.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412943984i/11445453.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <a href="http://warhawkevault.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415355089i/11776478.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<span id="freeTextContainer10857918063620167814"><b>✮✮✮✮ 4 tied stars✮✮✮✮<br/><br/><i>"Welcome to Albermarle Hall ...where all your darkest fantasies are made true..." </i></b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415003ra/818877.gif' width='500' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>'The tied up man ' is a basic angst story that involves the makings and breakings of an abused escort and about the danger of falling in love with someone with a damaged soul...<br/><br/><b>
  <i> “It was easy to forget that other people lived in a world where rules and laws and common sense could keep you safe. A world where, if you did the right thing you were allowed to get on with your life in whichever wa</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText10857918063620167814" style="display:none"><b>✮✮✮✮ 4 tied stars✮✮✮✮<br><br><i>"Welcome to Albermarle Hall ...where all your darkest fantasies are made true..." </i></b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380415003ra/818877.gif" width="500" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>'The tied up man ' is a basic angst story that involves the makings and breakings of an abused escort and about the danger of falling in love with someone with a damaged soul...<br><br><b>
  <i> “It was easy to forget that other people lived in a world where rules and laws and common sense could keep you safe. A world where, if you did the right thing you were allowed to get on with your life in whichever way you chose.”</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1400951708ra/9740759.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Initially while reading the summary &amp; 4 other star reviews ,I'm sure you would have figured out the bases of the plot while studiously raising ur expectations with every synonym of <b>'FANTASIC' 'MINDBLOWING' &amp; 'OUT OF THE WORLD'</b> present in the reviews.. Your pointer finger glides over the 'Favourite' button,ready to press down at the first indication of awesomeness before your even past the first few pages.....<br><br><b>A word of advice ? DONT DO THAT OK ?..Seriously..just dont.</b><br>**********************************************************************<br><u>
  <b>FIRST 50% :</b>
</u><br>Honestly when I first started this book ? I swear TO GOD I thought this read was going to be my first DNF book ever ! Seriously ask my trusty GR friend, Debra, I actually told her exactly that a day ago..Every page managed to bore me more than the last one,The main characters were to harsh &amp; snary,and the plot was absolutley wasted up to 50% of the whole book.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1432113924ra/14899571.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>**********************************************************************<br><b>
  <u>THE SECOND HALF: </u>
</b><br><br>LOL Now let's talk about the second half..The last 50% deserved every synonym of 'fantastic', 'unpredictable' &amp; smart you can find.Finally some awesomeness ! Alleluia ! <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1386623194ra/7407741.gif" width="400" height="260" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved how the plot twised and turned finally into a darker shade I was longing to see from the very beginning....I know some people have put this one there on the BDSM shelf ,but I don't really agree with that....<b>This book isn't really an erotica and NO its NOT THAT dark..</b>its more of suspense spy mission sorts actually.<br><br>*********************************************************************<br><br><b>
  <u>RECOMMENDATION:</u>
</b> This has been on my reading shelf for too long that I just had to pick this one and finish it off...as far as recommendation goes..<b>Tied Man</b> is Definatly a good read when ur in a mood for an emotional yet light.</span>

    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406624675p2/31339793.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1078943238?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/31339793-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jasmine by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/12206696-ilze">Ilze</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=buddy-recs">buddy-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=imma-hit-that-bitch">imma-hit-that-bitch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=there-be-crazy-mofos">there-be-crazy-mofos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=in-the-minority">in-the-minority</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=standalones">standalones</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=dark-deadly-dangerous">dark-deadly-dangerous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=im-gonna-need-therapy">im-gonna-need-therapy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31339793-jasmine?shelf=m-m-galore">m-m-galore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1078943238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11215825990409801079"><b>3 STARS! ★★★</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419688671ra/13113079.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Sorry guys but this is yet another less than stellar review from me. Honestly I'm trying to figure out if there's something wrong with me lately that I can't seem to shake out from this book funk. I had high hopes that this would be the one to pull me out since my fellow dark junkies rec'd me this & seeing everyone loving it. Sadly, it was not for me.<br/><br/>Again, this is another read that I didn't like but I didn't hate it either. Good news is that I found it to be a very refreshing read b</span>
  <span id="freeText11215825990409801079" style="display:none"><b>3 STARS! ★★★</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419688671ra/13113079.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sorry guys but this is yet another less than stellar review from me. Honestly I'm trying to figure out if there's something wrong with me lately that I can't seem to shake out from this book funk. I had high hopes that this would be the one to pull me out since my fellow dark junkies rec'd me this &amp; seeing everyone loving it. Sadly, it was not for me.<br><br>Again, this is another read that I didn't like but I didn't hate it either. Good news is that I found it to be a very refreshing read because the victim here happens to be a guy (hence, the title) and the villain is this crazy bitch who is so vile and sick to the head that I am <b>
  <i>appalled</i>
</b> that such a human being could go to that extent of depravity. Pretty sure she ain't human honestly.<br><br><u>And I will say this</u>: This book has some serious, <b>
  <i>
    <u>SERIOUS</u>
  </i>
</b> messed up and totally fucked up stuffs going on that could send people running for the hills or get a seizure from cringing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380410268ra/804254.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>But here's the problem for me. <b>I couldn't get into the writing style and when that happens, the book just...fails for me, no matter how much I found the story to be very well-written</b>. I loved the premise but the execution missed the mark for me. Don't get me wrong, the writing is eloquent and it was a little refreshing to see the usage of British slang. But after a while, it became an overkill with all the flowery prose that left me feeling detached from the read. I got lost between the dialogues and couldn't feel for these characters as much as I'd like to. In a way, that sucks because I kinda feel like a cold heartless bitch reading such a depraved, tortured read. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419689041ra/13113098.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, the paragraphs were so drawn out where 2 sentences would have sufficed instead of 2 full blown paragraphs. Added on with the slangs that threw me off, I ended up finding myself slowly getting bored with the read and skimming through :(<br><br><u>
  <b>Final verdict</b>
</u>: <b>This really is a case of "it's not you, it's me" problem.</b> I think the characters were well-developed, the premise was intriguing but the execution just didn't work for me. That being said, had it been written differently, I would have rated it higher. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11215825990409801079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/611863594" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer611863594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1954759577301455496"><br/><i>"Even though I walk through the valley of the shadow of death, I fear no evil, for You are with me ..."</i> Psalm 23:4<br/><br/>I am not a religious person but, while my mind was being thoroughly fucked as I was reading this book, that's what was going through my head.<br/><br/>This book is a true testament that women are much better at fucking with one's head than men ... If you happen to be familiar with "Consequences" and "The Dark Duet" books and thought those were hard to get through, to quote Bachman Turner, "you</span>
  <span id="freeText1954759577301455496" style="display:none"><br><i>"Even though I walk through the valley of the shadow of death, I fear no evil, for You are with me ..."</i> Psalm 23:4<br><br>I am not a religious person but, while my mind was being thoroughly fucked as I was reading this book, that's what was going through my head.<br><br>This book is a true testament that women are much better at fucking with one's head than men ... If you happen to be familiar with "Consequences" and "The Dark Duet" books and thought those were hard to get through, to quote Bachman Turner, "you ain't seen nothing yet" ... <br><br>To say this book was outstanding would be a ginormous understatement! I gave it 5 stars [because I thought "it was amazing"] when I was 60% into the story. I have to say though, I really hate myself for enjoying it because of it's subject matter but the writing is absolutely brilliant and the story, even though <i>very</i> hard to take, is incredible.<br><br>Surprisingly, I only managed to cry at acts of kindness in this book. I think I was too shocked to cry at other parts. <br><br>I don't think you really know evil till you meet Lady Blaine Albermarle. Books with this type of storyline don't usually get to me this much but what bothered me the most is that the villain in this case happens to be a woman who is also a mother. I am not sure why but this made her seem even more evil than she actually was (and I don't even know if that's possible!).<br><br>Tabitha McGowan, thank you for writing two of the most unforgettable characters &amp; incredibly sad yet very beautiful story about human kindness that will always prevail over evil!<br><br>Cheers!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424455516i/13763927._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 25379a67-51b6-487b-a141-474171f2617a_zpsff10c6eb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Get your copy:<br><br><a href="http://amzn.to/1Gconya" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon US</a><br><br><a href="http://amzn.to/1vOYkak" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon UK</a><br><br><a href="http://amzn.to/1Ad13j0" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon CA</a></b></span>
